the function must take in the current value of the\\n140:             :class:`AveragedModel` parameter, the current value of :attr:`model`\\n141:             parameter, and the number of models already averaged; if None,\\n142:             an equally weighted average is used (default: None)\\n143:         multi_avg_fn (function, optional): the averaging function used to update\\n144:             parameters inplace; the function must take in the current values of the\\n145:             :class:`AveragedModel` parameters as a list, the current values of :attr:`model`\\n146:             parameters as a list, and the number of models already averaged; if None,\\n147:             an equally weighted average is used (default: None)\\n148:         use_buffers (bool): if ``True``, it will compute running averages for\\n149:             both the parameters and the buffers of the model. (default: ``False``)\\n150: \\n151:     Example:\\n152:         >>> # xdoctest: +SKIP(\\\"undefined variables\\\")\\n153:         >>> loader, optimizer, model, loss_fn = ...\\n154:         >>> swa_model = torch.optim.swa_utils.AveragedModel(model)\\n155:         >>> scheduler = torch.optim.lr_scheduler.CosineAnnealingLR(optimizer,\\n156:         >>>                                     T_max=300)\\n157:         >>> swa_start = 160\\n158:         >>> swa_scheduler = SWALR(optimizer, swa_lr=0.05)\\n159:         >>> for i in range(300):\\n160:         >>>      for input, target in loader:\\n161:         >>>          optimizer.zero_grad()\\n162:         >>>          loss_fn(model(input), target).backward()\\n163:         >>>          optimizer.step()\\n164:         >>>      if i > swa_start:\\n165:         >>>          swa_model.update_parameters(model)\\n166:         >>>          swa_scheduler.step()\\n167:         >>>      else:\\n168:         >>>          scheduler.step()\\n169:         >>>\\n170:         >>> # Update bn statistics for the swa_model at the end\\n171:         >>> torch.optim.swa_utils.update_bn(loader, swa_model)\\n172: \\n173:     You can also use custom averaging functions with the `avg_fn` or `multi_avg_fn` parameters.\\n174:     If no averaging function is provided, the default is to compute\\n175:     equally-weighted average of the weights (SWA).\\n176: \\n177:     Example:\\n178:         >>> # xdoctest: +SKIP(\\\"undefined variables\\\")\\n179:         >>> # Compute exponential moving averages of the weights and buffers\\n180:         >>> ema_model = torch.optim.swa_utils.AveragedModel(model,\\n181:         >>>             torch.optim.swa_utils.get_ema_multi_avg_fn(0.9), use_buffers=True)\\n182: \\n183:     .. note::\\n184:         When using SWA/EMA with models containing Batch Normalization you may\\n185:         need to update the activation statistics for Batch Normalization.\\n186:         This can be done either by using the :meth:`torch.optim.swa_utils.update_bn`\\n187:         or by setting :attr:`use_buffers` to `True`. The first approach updates the\\n188:         statistics in a post-training step by passing data through the model. The\\n189:         second does it during the parameter update phase by averaging all buffers.\\n190:         Empirical evidence has shown that updating the statistics in normalization\\n191:         layers increases accuracy, but you may wish to empirically test which\\n192:         approach yields the best results in your problem.\\n193: \\n194:     .. note::\\n195:         :attr:`avg_fn` and `multi_avg_fn` are not saved in the :meth:`state_dict` of the model.\\n196: \\n197:     .. note::\\n198:         When :meth:`update_parameters` is called for the first time (i.e.\\n199:         :attr:`n_averaged` is `0`) the parameters of `model` are copied\\n200:         to the parameters of :class:`AveragedModel`. For every subsequent\\n201:         call of :meth:`update_parameters` the function `avg_fn` is used\\n202:         to update the parameters.\\n203: \\n204:     .. _Averaging Weights Leads to Wider     def get_lr(self):\\n460:         \\\"\\\"\\\"Get learning rate.\\\"\\\"\\\"\\n461:         # `_get_lr_called_within_step` is only available `_enable_get_lr_call`,\\n462:         # so we ignore the the function must take in the current value of the\\n140:             :class:`AveragedModel` parameter, the current value of :attr:`model`\\n141:             parameter, and the number of models already averaged; if None,\\n142:             an equally weighted average is used (default: None)\\n143:         multi_avg_fn (function, optional): the averaging function used to update\\n144:             parameters inplace; the function must take in the current values of the\\n145:             :class:`AveragedModel` parameters as a list, the current values of :attr:`model`\\n146:             parameters as a list, and the number of models already averaged; if None,\\n147:             an equally weighted average is used (default: None)\\n148:         use_buffers (bool): if ``True``, it will compute running averages for\\n149:             both the parameters and the buffers of the model. (default: ``False``)\\n150: \\n151:     Example:\\n152:         >>> # xdoctest: +SKIP(\\\"undefined variables\\\")\\n153:         >>> loader, optimizer, model, loss_fn = ...\\n154:         >>> swa_model = torch.optim.swa_utils.AveragedModel(model)\\n155:         >>> scheduler = torch.optim.lr_scheduler.CosineAnnealingLR(optimizer,\\n156:         >>>                                     T_max=300)\\n157:         >>> swa_start = 160\\n158:         >>> swa_scheduler = SWALR(optimizer, swa_lr=0.05)\\n159:         >>> for i in range(300):\\n160:         >>>      for input, target in loader:\\n161:         >>>          optimizer.zero_grad()\\n162:         >>>          loss_fn(model(input), target).backward()\\n163:         >>>          optimizer.step()\\n164:         >>>      if i > swa_start:\\n165:         >>>          swa_model.update_parameters(model)\\n166:         >>>          swa_scheduler.step()\\n167:         >>>      else:\\n168:         >>>          scheduler.step()\\n169:         >>>\\n170:         >>> # Update bn statistics for the swa_model at the end\\n171:         >>> torch.optim.swa_utils.update_bn(loader, swa_model)\\n172: \\n173:     You can also use custom averaging functions with the `avg_fn` or `multi_avg_fn` parameters.\\n174:     If no averaging function is provided, the default is to compute\\n175:     equally-weighted average of the weights (SWA).\\n176: \\n177:     Example:\\n178:         >>> # The first approach updates the\\n188:         statistics in a post-training step by passing data through the model. The\\n189:         second does it during the parameter update phase by averaging all buffers.\\n190:         Empirical evidence has shown that updating the statistics in normalization\\n191:         layers increases accuracy, but you may wish to empirically test which\\n192:         approach yields the best results in your problem.\\n193: \\n194:     .. note::\\n195:         :attr:`avg_fn` and `multi_avg_fn` are not saved in the :meth:`state_dict` of the model.\\n196: \\n197:     .. note::\\n198:         When :meth:`update_parameters` is called for the first time (i.e.\\n199:         :attr:`n_averaged` is `0`) the parameters of `model` are copied\\n200:         to the parameters of :class:`AveragedModel`. the function must take in the current value of the\n140:             :class:`AveragedModel` parameter, the current value of :attr:`model`\n141:             parameter, and the number of models already averaged; if None,\n142:             an equally weighted average is used (default: None)\n143:         multi_avg_fn (function, optional): the averaging function used to update\n144:             parameters inplace; the function must take in the current values of the\n145:             :class:`AveragedModel` parameters as a list, the current values of :attr:`model`\n146:             parameters as a list, and the number of models already averaged; if None,\n147:             an equally weighted average is used (default: None)\n148:         use_buffers (bool): if ``True``, it will compute running averages for\n149:             both the parameters and the buffers of the model. (default: ``False``)\n150: \n151:     Example:\n152:         >>> # xdoctest: +SKIP(\"undefined variables\")\n153:         >>> loader, optimizer, model, loss_fn = ...\n154:         >>> swa_model = torch.optim.swa_utils.AveragedModel(model)\n155:         >>> scheduler = torch.optim.lr_scheduler.CosineAnnealingLR(optimizer,\n156:         >>>                                     T_max=300)\n157:         >>> swa_start = 160\n158:         >>> swa_scheduler = SWALR(optimizer, swa_lr=0.05)\n159:         >>> for i in range(300):\n160:         >>>      for input, target in loader:\n161:         >>>          optimizer.zero_grad()\n162:         >>>          loss_fn(model(input), target).backward()\n163:         >>>          optimizer.step()\n164:         >>>      if i > swa_start:\n165:         >>>          swa_model.update_parameters(model)\n166:         >>>          swa_scheduler.step()\n167:         >>>      else:\n168:         >>>          scheduler.step()\n169:         >>>\n170:         >>> # Update bn statistics for the swa_model at the end\n171:         >>> torch.optim.swa_utils.update_bn(loader, swa_model)\n172: \n173:     You can also use custom averaging functions with the `avg_fn` or `multi_avg_fn` parameters.\n174:     If no averaging function is provided, the default is to compute\n175:     equally-weighted average of the weights (SWA).\n176: \n177:     Example:\n178:         >>> # xdoctest: +SKIP(\"undefined variables\")\n179:         >>> # Compute exponential moving averages of the weights and buffers\n180:         >>> ema_model = torch.optim.swa_utils.AveragedModel(model,\n181:         >>>             torch.optim.swa_utils.get_ema_multi_avg_fn(0.9), use_buffers=True)\n182: \n183:     .. note::\n184:         When using SWA/EMA with models containing Batch Normalization you may\n185:         need to update the activation statistics for Batch Normalization.\n186:         This can be done either by using the :meth:`torch.optim.swa_utils.update_bn`\n187:         or by setting :attr:`use_buffers` to `True`. The first approach updates the\n188:         statistics in a post-training step by passing data through the model. The\n189:         second does it during the parameter update phase by averaging all buffers.\n190:         Empirical evidence has shown that updating the statistics in normalization\n191:         layers increases accuracy, but you may wish to empirically test which\n192:         approach yields the best results in your problem.\n193: \n194:     .. note::\n195:         :attr:`avg_fn` and `multi_avg_fn` are not saved in the :meth:`state_dict` of the model.\n196: \n197:     .. note::\n198:         When :meth:`update_parameters` is called for the first time (i.e.\n199:         :attr:`n_averaged` is `0`) the parameters of `model` are copied\n200:         to the parameters of :class:`AveragedModel`. For every subsequent\n201:         call of :meth:`update_parameters` the function `avg_fn` is used\n202:         to update the parameters.\n203: \n204:     .. _Averaging Weights Leads to Wider Optima This line silences flake warnings\nload_tests = load_tests\n\n\nclass TestGradientNoiseInjector(TestCase):\n    \"\"\"Test suite for GradientNoiseInjector optimizer wrapper.\"\"\"\n\n    def setUp(self):\n        \"\"\"Set up test fixtures.\"\"\"\n        # Create a simple model\n        self.model = nn.Sequential(\n            nn.Linear(10, 20),\n            nn.ReLU(),\n            nn.Linear(20, 1),\n        )\n        self.loss_fn = nn.MSELoss()\n\n    def test_noise_injector_with_sgd(self):\n        \"\"\"Test that GradientNoiseInjector can wrap SGD optimizer.\"\"\"\n        base_optimizer = SGD(self.model.parameters(), lr=0.01)\n        optimizer = GradientNoiseInjector(base_optimizer, eta=0.01, gamma=0.55)\n\n        # Verify the optimizer wraps the SGD\n        self.assertIsInstance(optimizer.optimizer, SGD)\n        self.assertEqual(optimizer.eta, 0.01)\n        self.assertEqual(optimizer.gamma, 0.55)\n        self.assertEqual(optimizer.step_count, 0)\n\n    def test_noise_injector_with_adam(self):\n        \"\"\"Test that GradientNoiseInjector can wrap Adam optimizer.\"\"\"\n        base_optimizer = Adam(self.model.parameters(), lr=0.001)\n        optimizer = GradientNoiseInjector(base_optimizer, eta=0.01, gamma=0.55)\n\n        # Verify the optimizer wraps the Adam\n        self.assertIsInstance(optimizer.optimizer, Adam)\n\n    def test_noise_injection_occurs(self):\n        \"\"\"Test that noise is actually injected into gradients.\"\"\"\n        base_optimizer = SGD(self.model.parameters(), lr=0.01)\n        optimizer = GradientNoiseInjector(base_optimizer, eta=0.1, gamma=0.0)\n\n        # Forward pass\n        x = torch.randn(5, 10)\n        y = torch.randn(5, 1)\n        loss = self.loss_fn(self.model(x), y)\n\n        # Backward pass\n        optimizer.zero_grad()\n        loss.backward()\n\n        # Store original gradients\n        original_grads = [p.grad.clone() for p in self.model.parameters() if p.grad is not None]\n\n        # Step with noise injection\n        optimizer.step()\n\n        # Verify that gradients were modified during step\n        # (This is a bit tricky since we modify in-place and then step)\n        # So we'll check that step_count incremented\n        self.assertEqual(optimizer.step_count, 1)\n\n    def test_noise_variance_schedule(self):\n        \"\"\"Test that noise variance decays according to the schedule.\"\"\"\n        base_optimizer = SGD(self.model.parameters(), lr=0.01)\n        eta = 0.01\n        gamma = 0.55\n        optimizer = GradientNoiseInjector(base_optimizer, eta=eta, gamma=gamma)\n\n        x = torch.randn(5, 10)\n        y = torch.randn(5, 1)\n\n        # Simulate multiple steps and verify schedule\n        for step_idx in range(5):\n            self.model.zero_grad()\n            loss = self.loss_fn(self.model(x), y)\n            loss.backward()\n\n            # Verify the step_count before step\n            self.assertEqual(optimizer.step_count, step_idx)\n\n            # Expected variance at this step\n            expected_variance = eta / ((1 + step_idx) ** gamma)\n\n            # Step increments the step_count\n            optimizer.step()\n\n            # Verify step_count incremented\n            self.assertEqual(optimizer.step_count, step_idx + 1)\n\n    def test_zero_grad_delegation(self):\n        \"\"\"Test that zero_grad is correctly delegated to base optimizer.\"\"\"\n        base_optimizer = SGD(self.model.parameters(), lr=0.01)\n        optimizer = GradientNoiseInjector(base_optimizer)\n\n        x = torch.randn(5, 10)\n        y = torch.randn(5, 1)\n        loss = self.loss_fn(self.model(x), y)\n        loss.backward()\n\n        # Verify gradients exist\n        has_grads = any(p.grad is not None for p in self.model.parameters())\n        self.assertTrue(has_grads)\n\n        # Call zero_grad through wrapper\n        optimizer.zero_grad()\n\n        # Verify all gradients are zeroed\n        all_zero = all(\n            p.grad is None or torch.all(p.grad == 0)\n            for p in self.model.parameters()\n        )\n        self.assertTrue(all_zero)\n\n    def test_state_dict_save_load(self):\n        \"\"\"Test that state dict can be saved and loaded.\"\"\"\n        base_optimizer = SGD(self.model.parameters(), lr=0.01)\n        optimizer = GradientNoiseInjector(base_optimizer, eta=0.02, gamma=0.6)\n\n        x = torch.randn(5, 10)\n        y = torch.randn(5, 1)\n\n        # Take a few steps\n        for _ in range(3):\n            self.model.zero_grad()\n            loss = self.loss_fn(self.model(x), y)\n            loss.backward()\n            optimizer.step()\n\n        # Inject noise into all gradients\n        for group in self.optimizer.param_groups:\n            for param in group[\"params\"]:\n                if param.grad is not None:\n                    # Calculate noise variance based on current step count\n                    #
